I used to think posts about the loss of loved ones was pretty cringe. This was over a decade ago and I no longer feel the same so please don't misunderstand. I guess I was lucky, not having lost anyone since I was a teenager (45 now), but it seems like once the loss started, that it just has not stopped for me. Ive lost multiple loved ones just this year alone.  The one thing I have learned is that this is the one thing we will ALL have in common no matter what race, religion, political leanings, or any other divide you can think of. It's something we must all learn to live with and it will never be easy to do so. Death is the great unifier. It may be painful for us who have to live with the loss but it isbeautiful for the ones who pass and undergo the greatest journey of their lives.  So if it makes you feel better to post a comment about it, rest assured that those of us in the know will read your comments with great diligence, compassion and understanding. If you're onthe fence just go for it. Feel better. Seek closure. Gain support, even if it is from a stranger. You don't have to be alone with these struggles.  â¤

Cosmic
It's no accident that A7X's best songs are like a long journey...many separate parts, melodies and tempos arranged into a masterpiece.  One of the few bands out there with the balls to stray from the 3.5 minute verse/chorus/verse/hook formula and really risk it all to experiment and play what they feel.  Clearly, it resonates.  While they are truly at their best with the heavy stuff with hooks and payoffs, almost nobody does these epic songs better.  Showcases perfectly why 20 years ago a lot of us knew they'd stay evolving and stay at the top.

Crazy that the Stage is already 7 years old. I like this version of avenged
I'm in Grad School for my MA in English: Creative Writing. I say this because when I was a teenager I was suffering from severe undiagnosed depression. i thought maybe it was just some phase that I would look back on and roll my eyes with. Looking back, and how it took me drastically changing my life for me to escape it, there was more going on. So when I first heard this album, it captured all my worries, fears, anxieties, and dread from that time of my life before I swapped to English as my major. Every single song. Game Over, Mattel, Nobody, We Love You, every single one captured an emotion, a thought, a feeling. Except this one. Cosmic feels like the only one that feels like a song in my current stage of life. And while there are many interpretations, this song reminds me of my current girlfriend and I and our backgrounds. How many times where if our lives diverted just slightly, we probably still would have met. We both admitted it felt like an inevitability and somehow God brought us together. So even though this song is about the death of a loved one and meeting again in another life, that's how this relationship feels. Like we'll always meet again somehow. This song makes me tear up more often than not.  Edit 7 months later: 11/04/2024. Turns out she cheated on me a few months before this video and I found out through the guy she cheated on me with. She tried to break it off with him as a fling, but the damage was done. At that time we were 3 years together.  She may feel guilt, but that's on her. Maybe in another time or life we would have worked, but not in this one.

Man, this has such intense Terry Pratchett vibes.
It's a beautiful music video, one of the most stunning to look at of all of them, full of meanings and emotions, but I feel somewhat put off that there isn't very much Avenged Sevenfold of it. As with the Nobody music video, there's skeletal imagery, which is in-character enough for A7X, though not a Deathbat, or anything which indicates that it's an A7X music video specifically. The Nobody music video works extremely well to portray that song because it isn't like any other music video, it has details of Life Is but a Dream...  's themes, and it's so rich of what it elaborates on. I'm not convinced that this music video portrays A7X's music, so much as Chris Hopewell's perspectives of death and existence within his lens of this song as he considers his presentation and not A7X's. Wes Lang has at least painted Deathbats and logos for the band, Mattel's music video by Zoe Katz has clear humor of A7X, and hidden references, so other artists convey abstractions of Life Is but a Dream...  without diminishing A7X's presence of it, but this music video feels adjacent of A7X. Including bat wings on the Grim Reaper could've made it immediately apparent that it's A7X related. As it is, a great number of other songs could be played over it and it would match them equally, because it's common. It isn't distinctly A7X, distinctly Cosmic as a song, or distinctly iconic. I appreciate efforts which had went into it, though for me, it isn't a music video which I'll watch much, any more than a visualizer. I'm grateful to have followed its premiere, and I look forward to every present moment of A7X.

Rarely am I afraid to listen to or watch a song again. Many people rightfully love this, but I think few actually understand yet. I'm among those who were allowed to remember a piece of the everything... the immersive illusion of the dream makes you forget, but triggers like this let you remember briefly. I don't want to get into details but in her final days on hospice she couldn't move, eat, walk, or talk. I played all her favorite A7x songs while she was in bed.  She never heard this song before so I played it at the end of the playlist. She passed away that morning and this was the last song she ever listened to. To say this song has meaning to me is an understatement. The fact it was written during her illness and was the last song she heard. It makes me cry every time but with mixed emotions.  Sadness but knowing she's at peace. I think the flipping of the hourglass at the end symbolizes that even though our loved ones who passed are waiting for us they want us to continue to live our lives to the fullest.  I love you with all my heart Kristinaâ¤. She was 33 years old.

This album taught me an important lesson. When it came out I hated it... I was expecting the same band that made City of Evil, but somewhere around the third listen, I realized how narrow minded and just plain stupid that was. This is a band that has grown and changed just as much as I have grown and changed. It wasn't fair to expect that they wouldn't change. Now this is one of my favorite albums of any band and I have listened to it through close to 100 times, far more than any prior A7X album. Now I listen to each album as a new thing and I don't compare them to the past anymore. I have fallen in love with music again.

I lost my 19 year old son, Jacob, to Osteosarcoma in October of 2023.  A very rare form of bone cancer that only affects 3 out of every million people.  He loved Avenged Sevenfold and I prayed that he would live long enough to be able to hear Life is But a Dream, as we followed it's production over his 2 year battle.  Thankfully the album released in 2023 and he loved it.  I took him to the Camden NJ show in a wheelchair on July 18, 2023 and it was my favorite memory with my son.  He wore an Avenged Sevenfold tshirt at his funeral and he was buried in it.  His prayer card has verses from the song So Far Away on it.  Thanks to the band for a night we will never forget and for bringing my son and I closer together.

My aunt who i was super close with, passed away two weeks ago from colon cancer. We LOVED A7X, I actually got my music taste from her. She raised me on classic metal, ozzy, pretty much everything from the 80s and 70s, the start of metal. When i found out she liked a7x too it brought us so much closer. The skeleton dancing made me happy, because not only did she have colon cancer but she was paralyzed from the waste down to to her ex husband shooting her when i was 6 years old. When she died, i know wherever it is we go when we die she was dancing. Hopefully to the rev playing some kick ass drums.  The day she died i passed her old apartment she hadnt lived there in ten years, but as i passed it Far Away started playing and it made me cry. But now i have this song to imagine how happy and pain free she is, and i can remember the amazing times i had with her.
